< text>
For the premium prices you pay to live in a "luxury" apartment complex, you'd certainly expect a higher degree of communication with tenants, especially during uncertain times like these. However, tenants have been consistently blindsided by management's decisions time after time. The entire complex was rebranded overnight from Millennium Mission Valley to Metro Mission Valley in the middle of a pandemic with ZERO explanation. Amenities were abruptly reopened after over 2 months of closure, but only from 9am-5pm (y'know, when most people are at work and unable to use them). Cars parked in visitor parking were broken into **inside the structure**, with no response except a new sign posted claiming no liability for stolen items. A tenant's car spontaneously burst into flames right outside some apartments without a word. Management couldn't be bothered to communicate increased safety measures or major changes by email, but is quite diligent in posting physical letters to our doors to let us know we don't qualify for rent control or that our lease is up for renewal.

I understand pandemics are out of their control, but the corporate greed and blatant lack of compassion during these trying times is disappointing to say the least. Residents continued to pay full rent prices for amenities we could not access--the pool, the sports lounge, the clubhouse, the business center, the coffee machines, the fitness center, the yoga studio--and were refused any rent credits during this time.

For those sensitive to noise, please note that ongoing construction next door has kept our apartments noisy and literally vibrating all day long.

If you're looking for a nice place to call home, I suggest you look elsewhere. You've been warned.</text>

<Text>Shout out to some of the leasing staff, and the efficient and cool cats of the maintenance staff. They have been great in addressing our concerns when talking with me directly.

Unfortunately, there are too many factors at play that merit my rating. We had bugs initially when we moved in, but the fumigation by the apartment service didn't really work and the fumes lingered for much longer than what is probably healthy for a 1-year-old. We ended up buying bug traps from the department store and that solved the problem... bugs are back though (mainly ants now) and I'm sure buying more traps is an affordable and easy solution.

The construction is bothersome, and was definitely not communicated well. It's unfortunate, but with how much I'm paying for my unit (more than  $3K), it has been awful raising a family when construction wakes the household up. The shaking of the foundations and appliances went on for a good week or so too, so that was a bummer to wake up to. There is really no schedule for what to expect every morning with regard to the noise, so teleworking from home has been painful to say the least... wish I could use the business center.

The Sonder occupants rule our floor, so not being residents, they don't share the same courtesy that other residents do. Music is played loudly, there's excessive noise that must be related to a small room party (?), odors of smoked substances waft the hall outside some of their doors, and they must not be directed in how to throw away trash, because we had instances (more than once) in which our valet trash was used to throw away their food. We had pizza and ice cream once that resulted in ants outside of our door in the morning.

The elevators are conveniently inaccessible when you need them the most, and no notice is given until you find that you need to use it. Staircase doors on different floors remain locked, and some aren't at random times. It's nonsensical, but the roaming security guard says they should all be locked. They have access control proximity readers on the entrances downstairs, so I don't understand the inconvenience it takes to go to the desired floor, instead of using the appropriate door, you walk through the garage and across the way, enter the unlocked double doors and you essentially have the same access to the hallway as if you entered through the locked stair door.

Additionally, the amenities have been inaccessible due to the pandemic, but no compensation was offered or granted upon asking. They continued to clean the various amenities (community lounge(s), business center, kids playroom, gym, pool, etc.) but wouldn't even do controlled access. This has lasted for months. Now that the gym and pool are opening up, there's only guidance to maintain social distance, but even then, the other amenities are still closed off. My yearly rent will not increase, but it's obvious by shopping around online that my unit is being offered at a lower value for new sign-ups. This was the final nail in the coffin.

Anyway, it's not hard to find an equivalent place with the same amenities but with a more understanding and communicative company. Probably more affordable than what I got roped into as well.< /Text><Pics>None< /Pics>< response>

R&V Management is the problem.
PREMIUM AMENTITIES NO LONGER AVAILABLE FOR THE FORESEEABLE FUTURE

Moving to Metro Mission Valley apartments, or Millennium Mission Valley as it was known last December was a no brainer. Mission Valley is 15 minutes from everywhere, lots of great restaurants and shopping and a pretty scenic river walk. The building and staff have always been great and the PREMIUM AMENTITIES were hard to pass up. Great lounge areas, pool, and 2 floor weight room, and countless other places to hang, relax, and meet neighbors.

After the onset of COVID 19 , states, business, and apartments made necessary and well timed changes to common areas and amenities and Metro Mission Valley was no different. The staff have remained on hand and continue to be professional, courteous, and great and I‚Äôm glad that our rent continues to ensure these great people have jobs and security.

However the similarities to surrounding apartments stopped there. R&V Management was mum to address concerns of timing or providing information concerning the opening of common areas we all pay for. It was only after a group of neighbors organized into a tenet association that management bothered to respond to questions. To make matters worse, R&V Management has refused to meet tenets requests in providing any concessions to help our neighbors or reward tenet loyalty, either with rent credits or rent increase freezes. Instead R&V Management has shut down dialogue and further inquiry with responses from their lawyers, leaving PREMIUM AMENITIES unused, and still very much paid for. It is unacceptable that R&V Management continues to ignore established tenets concerns and help lighten the load of a burden that has taken a costly toll on the community at large.

For NEW AND PROSPECTIVE TENETS, you should be aware of R&V Managements inability to be flexible or empathetic, especially in the context of a pandemic that IS showing signs of a second round of infections and possible shutdowns. Great introductory prices for PREMIUM AMENITIES sounds too good to be true. And it is.< /review>

< Review>
The best place l have ever rented from.

l have lived in apartments that have claimed to be luxury but none have lived up to being "luxury", until this one. Some of the things that drew me in were the amenities like the pool area, the onsite BBQ grills, complimentary coffee machines, common areas with billiards, large flatscreens, and game cabinet. The apartments are amazing with beautiful dark cabinets and complementary stainless steel appliances. In apartment washers and dryers may have been the thing that sold me on this apartment.

I am within walking distance to a Trader Joes, two malls with movie theaters, and great restaurants. Access to the interstate is fast, I can be on l-8 in under a minute most mornings. The community is quiet and I forget that it is next to the Interstate when sitting outside.

This is a great place to live in San Diego.</Review>

<Pics>None<//Pics><review>After 12 years, it was time to replace the HVAC system in my 60 year-old house.  And I found myself in the same situation you're currently in -- there are so many air conditioning and heating companies in the valley, where do you even begin?

What I did was this:  I gave myself a big wide swath of time, I made a list of things I wanted out of a new HVAC system, I did my research and I got bids from everyone.  I can honestly say that I immersed myself in the terrifying underworld of conditioned air, and I can unequivocally recommend the folks at Timo's.

They were not the cheapest bid -- but they weren't the most expensive, either; you can entertain a wide range of prices when it comes to HVAC depending on your needs, and one of the things I appreciated about the folks at Timo's was their willingness to say when something wasn't needed or excessive.  They provided a new compressor, a new furnace, entirely new ductwork, a new low-voltage wire, and a digital thermostat; I added additional filtration and upgraded the registers, which they easily accommodated, and I also had they blow new insulation into a small attic area -- the end result is that everything is new, it works beautifully and it was all almost surgically placed within the confines of my home.

But what really made the difference, in my estimation, were the people I encountered who work for Timo's -- beyond always being on time and doing the job well, every single man and woman I encountered approached the job with enthusiasm and a sense of, well, fun.  It was fun for them to be updating an old house and an old house's system; they were excited to be doing it and they were excited to see what I thought when it was done.  The men and women who work for Joe TImo know the difference they're making in their customers' lives, and they really celebrate it.
